href="https://unsplash.com/ko/@markkoenig?utm_content=creditCopyText&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_source=unsplash" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Mark König</a> on <a class="af oq" href="https://unsplash.com/ko/%EC%82%AC%EC%A7%84/%EB%B9%A8%EA%B0%84%EC%83%89%EA%B3%BC-%EA%B2%80%EC%9D%80-%EC%83%89-%EA%B0%9C-%EA%B0%84%ED%8C%90-mx94V7uE1eU?utm_content=creditCopyText&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_source=unsplash" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Unsplash</a></figcaption></figure><h1 id="9da5" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Executive Summary</h1><ul class=""><li id="e77b" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">S2W threat research and intelligence center <strong class="my gv">Talon</strong> has hunted for and analyzed a sample of what is believed to be a new malware from the Kimsuky group on VirusTotal.</li></ul><p id="b7ee" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">— The malware was found to be distributed from a page that redirects users to a specific site located in South Korea to download a security program.</p><p id="81e7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">— Unlike typical supply chain attacks, only 2 of the 5 installers distributed by the site were modified to include the malware.</p><ul class=""><li id="a92d" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">The hunted malware is an Info-stealer malware written in Go language that steals information from the infected system, which is dropped and executed from a Dropper disguised as a security program installation file (TrustPKI, NX_PRNMAN) from SGA Solutions.</li><li id="71cb" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">The dropper runs as a legitimate installer alongside the malware, and both the dropper and malware are signed with <strong class="my gv">a valid, legitimate “D2innovation Co.,LTD” certificate</strong>, suggesting that the company’s certificate was actually stolen.</li><li id="cd56" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">S2W Talon has named the malware “<strong class="my gv">Troll Stealer</strong>” because it contains the pathname “D:/~/repo/golang/src/root.go/s/<strong class="my gv">troll</strong>/agent” within the malware.</li><li id="8798" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">(Behaviors)</strong> Troll Stealer can steal information from the infected system like SSH, FileZilla, C drive files/directories, browser, system information, screen captures and send it to the C&amp;C server.</li><li id="c50d" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">(Attribution)</strong> Based on the Kimsuky group’s recent active use of Go-based malware, and the fact that Troll Stealer contains a lot of code similar to the AppleSeed and AlphaSeed malware associated with the Kimsuky group, we speculate that the Kimsuky group is behind the distribution of this malware.</li></ul><p id="c070" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">— However, there is also a possibility that another group closely associated with the Kimsuky group is behind the malware, as we have identified some differences in the TTPs from those previously observed from the Kimsuky group.</p><ul class=""><li id="7b17" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">(Target)</strong> Troll Stealer includes the ability to steal the GPKI folder on infected systems, which suggests that the campaign may have been targeting devices within administrative and public organizations in South Korea.</li></ul><p id="8f4a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">— However, there are some differences in the TTP from the Kimsuky group’s previous TTPs, suggesting that another group closely associated with the Kimsuky group may be behind this campaign.</p><ul class=""><li id="d137" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">In addition to Troll Stealer, <strong class="my gv">additional malware signed with the same legitimate certificate was found</strong>, so malware signed with that certificate may be distributed in the future.</li></ul><h1 id="b2d9" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Introduction</h1><p id="6929" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">On January 10, 2024, a Go language-based information-stealing malware was discovered and we conducted a detailed analysis. The malware was distributed from a security program download page that was redirected when accessing a specific website in Korea and disguised as a security program installation file (TrustPKI, NX_PRNMAN) of SGA Solutions.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qc"><picture><source “D:/~/repo/golang/src/root.go/s/<strong class="my gv">troll</strong>/agent”.</p><h1 id="0a49" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Detailed Malware execution flow</figcaption></figure><h2 id="4aaf" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">Stage1. Dropper</h2><p id="4d02" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">1. Mutex &amp; Self-deletion</strong></p><p id="6398" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">When executed, it creates a mutex to prevent duplicate execution and subsequently creates and executes a BAT script file in the %Temp% subpath for self-deletion.</p><p id="bf1b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Mutex name</strong>: windows update {2024–1020–02A}</p><ul class=""><li id="087c" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">File path</strong>: %Temp%\\[A-Z0–9]{4}.tmp.bat</li><li id="bad4" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">BAT file contents</strong></li></ul><pre class="ob oc od oe of qw qx qy bp qz bb bk"><span id="dc95" class="ra os gu qx b bg rb rc l rd re">:goto_redel<br/>rd /s /q [File path]<br/>del [File path]<br/>if exist [File path] goto goto_redel<br/>del %Temp%\\[A-Z0-9]{4}.tmp.bat</span></pre><p id="e9e3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">2. Execute Normal Installer (</strong>NXTPKIENTS.exe)</p><p id="853b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Then drop and run a legitimate installation file from SGA Solutions in the Desktop path. Paths where information-stealing malware is dropped and filenames for infection history checks</figcaption></figure><p id="e369" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Troll Stealer is then executed via the rundll32.exe process, which calls the same Export function as the filename used for the infection check. The malware was packed with VMProtect to prevent analysis.</p><ul class=""><li id="04bf" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Command</strong>: C:\Windows\system32\rundll32.exe %AppData%\[DLL Path] [Export]</li></ul><h2 id="7859" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">Stage2. Troll Stealer</h2><ul class=""><li id="626e" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Filename</strong>: C:\Users\admin\AppData\Roaming\Hancom\hc-[a-z0–9]{8}.png</li><li id="2fce" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">MD5</strong>: 88f183304b99c897aacfa321d58e1840</li><li id="b8a6" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">SHA256</strong>: 61b8fbea8c0dfa337eb7ff978124ddf496d0c5f29bcb5672f3bd3d6bf832ac92</li><li id="11cf" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Type</strong>: DLL</li></ul><p id="c39c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">1. Initial behavior</strong></p><p id="0276" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">During its initial execution, it deletes the “ChromeUpdateTaskMachineUAC” scheduler. However, given that Troll Stealer and its parent Dropper do not have the feature to register a scheduler with the above name, it is likely that it did not accidentally remove a feature that was used in the past.</p><ul class=""><li id="3663" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Command</strong>: schtasks /delete /f /tn “ChromeUpdateTaskMachineUAC”</li></ul><p id="40ef" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The malware then checks for the existence of the file to check the infection dropped by the dropper malware to determine if it was executed via a dropper. It performs malicious behavior only if the file exists.</p><ul class=""><li id="35c9" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">File path</strong>: %ProgramData%\limsjo.a</li></ul><p id="6954" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Stealer itself registers mutexes to prevent malware duplicate execution.</p><ul class=""><li id="0fcb" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Mutex name</strong>: chrome development kit 1.0</li></ul><p id="c926" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">2. Set configuration data</strong></p><p id="50be" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It collects the MAC address and directory path of the infected system and creates a temporary file with configured data for later malicious behavior. Configuration contains information such as C&amp;C server addresses.</p><ul class=""><li id="99ee" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Configuration path</strong>: %UserProfile%\.tmp\{Random Number}.org</li><li id="3d43" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">C&amp;C server</strong>: hxxp[:]//qi.limsjo.p-e[.]kr/index.php</li><li id="20fe" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu Data collection</strong></p><p id="912c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Troll Stealer steals various information from the infected system, encrypts it, and sends it to the C&amp;C server. The malware steals the following information</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz rv"><picture><source Target data and encrypted filename</figcaption></figure><p id="dfde" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3.1. SSH</p><p id="9848" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It exfiltrates the infected system’s SSH information. It compresses the system’s <em class="nx">.ssh</em> directory and creates a file. Afterward, it encrypts the compressed file, creates a file in a different path, and sends it to the C&amp;C server.</p><ul class=""><li id="46f3" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">.SSH directory save path</strong>: %USERPROFILE%\.ssh</li><li id="8a5a" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Encrypted file path</strong>: %AppData%\local\tsd@{YYMMDD}(HH.MM.SS-000).gte1</li></ul><p id="c487" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3.2. FileZilla</p><p id="9c32" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It exfiltrates information from FileZilla software present on the infected system. It compresses the <em class="nx">filezilla</em> directory and creates a file. The compressed file is then encrypted and created as a file in a different path and sent to the C&amp;C server.</p><ul class=""><li id="d414" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">FileZilla directory save Path</strong>: %AppData%\filezilla</li><li id="0380" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Encrypted file path</strong>: %AppData%\local\tfd@{YYMMDD}(HH.MM.SS-000).gte1</li></ul><p id="e481" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3.3. Microsoft Sticky Note</p><p id="2103" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It exfiltrates information from Microsoft Sticky Note present on the infected system. It compresses the <em class="nx">localstate</em> directory and creates a file. The compressed file is then encrypted and created as a file in a different path and sent to the C&amp;C server.</p><ul class=""><li id="c92c" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Microsoft Sticky Note save path</strong>: %USERPROFILE%\AppData\Local\packages\microsoft.microsoftstickynotes_8wekyb3d8bbwe\localstate</li><li id="618e" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Encrypted file path</strong>: %AppData%\local\tnd@{YYMMDD}(HH.MM.SS-000).gte1</li></ul><p id="70b3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3.4. “GPKI” directory in C Drive</p><p id="6f90" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Troll Stealer steals data from a specific folder on the C drive of an infected system. The attacker collects the names of files and folders on the C drive and appends additional strings to create a new string, as shown below. It then generates a SHA512 hash of that string, and if it is the same as the hardcoded SHA512 hash in the malware, it encrypts the file and sends it to the C&amp;C server. Analyzing the hardcoded SHA512 hash revealed that the attacker attempted to steal the <strong class="my gv">GPKI</strong> folder on the C drive.</p><ul class=""><li id="1967" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">String format</strong>: “aaxxyyzz” + {File name} + “zzyyxxaa”</li></ul><p id="3854" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">==&gt; Target string</strong>: aaxxyyzz<strong class="my gv">gpki</strong>zzyyxxaa</p><ul class=""><li id="1145" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Hardcoded SHA512 hash in Troll Stealer</strong>: 17ccb0832c3382b5f9e86236e035d899a351c98f3871080c138d4494218cbbc2b6f9dc43705ed97e8b0b09f25752302094e0d297151f67b22328af95610f72f1</li><li id="f4e3" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Encrypted file path</strong>: %AppData%\local\tcd@{YYMMDD}(HH.MM.SS-000).gte1</li></ul><p id="364d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">GPKI, also known as an administrative electronic signature certificate, is an authorized certificate used to verify the authenticity of administrative electronic signatures, which is used by governments such as administrative and public institutions in South Korea. In other words, it is not used on ordinary computers but is usually installed on computers used for public affairs. In this regard, it is believed that this campaign is aimed at targeting PCs installed in public.</p><p id="4a3b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3.5. Browser Information</p><p id="65b2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It steals browser information from the infected system. The malware is believed to have utilized <a class="af oq" href="https://github.com/moonD4rk/HackBrowserData" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">HackBrowserData</a>, an open-source program written in Go language, to steal browser information. It targets Chromium-based browsers and Firefox browsers on infected systems and steals various information such as cookies, history, downloads, and extensions and saves them as JSON files in the browser directory. After compressing the browser directory, it performs encryption and sends it to the C&amp;C server.</p><ul class=""><li id="ed9f" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Browser save</strong> <strong class="my gv">path</strong>: %AppData%\local\browser</li><li id="263f" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Encrypted file path</strong>: %AppData%\local\tbd@{YYMMDD}(HH.MM.SS-000).gte1</li></ul><p id="4f33" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3.6. System Information</p><p id="982e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It steals system information from an infected system. It collects infected system information through CMD commands, encrypts it, and creates a file. The encrypted file is sent to the C&amp;C server.</p><ul class=""><li id="82e8" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Encrypted file path</strong>: %AppData%\local\ccmd@{YYMMDD}(HH.MM.SS-000).gte1</li></ul><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj List of system information collected</figcaption></figure><ul class=""><li id="fffb" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Commands to collect system information</strong></li></ul><pre class="ob oc od oe of qw qx qy bp qz bb bk"><span id="aedc" class="ra os gu qx b bg rb rc l rd re">systeminfo &amp; <br/>net user &amp; <br/>query user &amp; <br/>powershell Get-CimInstance -Namespace root/SecurityCenter2 -Classname AntivirusProduct &amp; <br/>wmic qfe &amp; <br/>wmic startup get &amp; <br/>wmic logicaldisk get &amp; <br/>ipconfig /all &amp; <br/>arp -a &amp; <br/>route print &amp; <br/>tasklist &amp; <br/>wmic process get Caption, Commandline &amp; <br/>dir &quot;%programfiles%&quot; &amp; <br/>dir &quot;%programfiles% (x86)&quot; &amp; <br/>dir &quot;%programdata%\Microsoft\Windows\Start Menu\Programs&quot; &amp; <br/>dir &quot;%appdata%\Microsoft\Windows\Recent&quot; &amp; <br/>dir /s &quot;%userprofile%\desktop&quot; &amp; <br/>dir /s &quot;%userprofile%\downloads&quot; &amp; <br/>dir /s &quot;%userprofile%\documents&quot;</span></pre><p id="48b5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">3.7. Screen Capture</p><p id="c6b6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Capture the current desktop screen of the infected machine and save it to a file. Use the screenshot package of “<a class="af oq" href="https://github.com/kbinani/screenshot" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">kbinani</a>” published on Github to capture the desktop screen. Encrypt the captured file and create a file, then send the encrypted file to the C&amp;C server.</p><ul class=""><li id="481f" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Encrypted file path</strong>: %AppData%\local\ssht@{YYMMDD}(HH.MM.SS-000).gte1</li></ul><p id="accf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">4. File Encryption</strong></p><p id="4b98" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Before sending the stolen data to the C&amp;C server, it encrypts the data using a combination of RC4 and RSA-4096 algorithms. The malware parses the RSA public key from the hardcoded DER of PKCS#1. It then randomly generates an RC4 key value and uses it to encrypt the stolen data. The RC4 encryption key is encrypted with the RSA public key.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz du">Figure 6. Encryption flow before file transfer</figcaption></figure><ul class=""><li id="9dad" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Hardcoded PKCS#1 DER</strong></li></ul><pre class="ob oc od oe of qw qx qy bp qz bb bk"><span id="bac5" class="ra os gu qx b bg rb rc l rd re">3082020a0282020100c3fc0e50f4dcafec48ee42362d70c8f6b3153e91566b15a9540d0ca9f3e81846093d8752940b414043c0eaa752dd29b3aa7132bc3a1c9d8c8ed8aeaeb51c1ab99491879e8e9af96eec3f87d64fdc6dc2e51bed259314c6417d481472463a3df1ca5a16254f203aecb10c56e0dc0b8f9f6e70cc286161dbd2d0e6e3652a438ba1e48cc822cb2138f012e4cd4132c627ca165a17793785fc4c74198b03bcd8743f389345edb4238984ebf84d9a89851b5adc6378a4c0b441bab7f7e15330be4ed3abadb393cce9a3f1e37cf71cbbf3cc32c2b399cdc2cd65f651be21ef84c9bf67c13cbd38a0d0897dfc1f6b7ba809ef59f5de9019697115ddfdae5cb885f78e4766af4c23c95ebb198656ee391d788ab52fd760670561d417f099538f45f652b438b5b32afa0c2ae08eb04381112a254aff4e6eeb1db29be8dc248a85226a21528e87b837801f7a81ab4e0b03d0b23ba8c69bad52d094c343444676b9d1516cf3cf1017942cf12eadc16cf56f843ba344deb6c7e935b4abf574d8121b301dc05ce7945578ede2f14be9daab4bd6be430dcf7f4e39e97fba7f462822c6743ac8dc79674dcd5c958c94bf27490758e9fa13432e5f0134cacd422115a0e76fcfd14b9b86f88bb3e136fc54c46ea6d2212ea00478dc11d9cf80c06fab2c4a3c7d3ad5f4fa00f4999a2170189eb747368e41c2cf41302e476c39861876512d9f8d355b0203010001</span></pre><p id="bd73" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">5. C&amp;C Communication</strong></p><p id="be9b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The malware creates a 60-byte structure and organizes 12 fields to exfiltrate the Config data and data stolen from the victim system. The value of each field is set differently depending on the purpose of the communication and the type of data to be transmitted, and the payload is located after the size_payload field. The configured data is XORed and Base64 encoded and sent to the C&amp;C server through the HTTP protocol. The common structure for communication is shown in <em class="nx">Figure 7</em>, and the meaning of each field is described in <em class="nx">Table 5</em>.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz Data computation process</figcaption></figure><p id="e898" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The final stolen data is sent as follows:</p><ul class=""><li id="0c60" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Steal data =&gt; Encrypt file(RC4+RSA) =&gt; Encode structure used for communication(XOR+Base64) =&gt; Pass as <strong class="my gv"><em class="nx">a</em></strong> parameter</li></ul><p id="d7a4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Troll Stealer sends the “init” string in the payload to the C&amp;C server only the first time it communicates, and only when it receives the “ok” string in response does it continue to leak the stolen data.</p><p id="c812" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In this case, there are a total of four communications per exfiltration of configuration or stolen items: the first communication is to perform the ping function, and the second and third communications are sent with the same data in the payload. However, we can see that the value of the <em class="nx">status_type</em> field is configured differently. Finally, the fourth communication includes the stolen filename in the payload and sets the value of the <em class="nx">send_type</em> field to 5. Once the file is successfully sent to the C&amp;C server, delete the encrypted file in the %appdata%\local\ path.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz ry"><picture><source srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/1*n8QkQ3uh76hRJvBvNB1gLA.png 640w, Communication flow for Troll Stealer</figcaption></figure><p id="ada4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">6. Self-deletion</strong></p><p id="7146" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">After executing the malware, it creates a PS1 file in the <em class="nx">.tmp</em> directory and runs it via the powershell.exe, which deletes Troll Stealer itself.</p><ul class=""><li id="2173" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">.PS1 save path</strong>: %USERPROFILE%\.tmp\{Random}.ps1</li><li id="a93b" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Command</strong>: powershell.exe -executionpolicy bypass -File [ps1 file]</li><li id="127f" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">.PS1 file contents</strong></li></ul><pre class="ob oc od oe of qw qx qy bp qz bb bk"><span id="a75d" class="ra os gu qx b bg rb rc l rd re">$target = {Stealer Path}<br/>for ($i = 0; $i -lt 50; $i++)<br/>{<br/> Remove-Item $target -Force<br/> Remove-Item $PSCommandPath -Force<br/> if (!(Test-Path $target) -and !(Test-Path $PSCommandPath))<br/> {<br/>  break<br/> }<br/> Start-Sleep -Seconds 2<br/>}</span></pre><h1 id="aead" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Attribution</h1><p id="ed8e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">S2W speculates that the Kimsuky group may be behind the distribution of this malware based on the group’s recent active use of Go-based malware and the similarity of the code to existing AppleSeed and AlphaSeed malware.</p><h2 id="63b2" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">Correlation with AppleSeed/AlphaSeed</h2><p id="63a2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">The path that the dropper malware drops Troll Stealer and the filename format it creates appear similar to the path and filename of AppleSeed, which was disclosed by <a class="af oq" href="https://asec.ahnlab.com/ko/28741/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">ASEC</a>.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div The encryption/decryption method used by AlphaSeed and Troll Stealer.</figcaption></figure><p id="3383" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Furthermore, the Go language library used to capture the victim system’s desktop screen was identified as the same kbinani package also used by AlphaSeed.</p><ul class=""><li id="0b64" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><a class="af oq" href="https://github.com/kbinani/screenshot" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">https://github.com/kbinani/screenshot</a></li></ul><h2 id="c5aa" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">Another golang-based backdoor (GoBear)</h2><p id="32de" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">In addition to the Troll Stealer, another Go language-based backdoor malware signed with a legitimate “D2innovation Co.,LTD certificate” was also found.</p><ul class=""><li id="cce9" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">MD5</strong>: 87429e9223d45e0359cd1c41c0301836</li><li id="0a5a" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">C&amp;C</strong>: hxxp[:]//coolsystem[.]co.kr/admin/mail/index.php</li><li id="f112" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Reference</strong>: <a class="af oq" href="https://zhuanlan.zhihu.com/p/680534132" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Kimsuky (APT-Q-2) secret theft operation disguised as software installation package</a></li></ul><p id="8ea6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The malware performs malicious behaviors based on the commands it receives from the C&amp;C server, and the strings contained in the names of the functions it calls have been found to overlap with the commands used by <strong class="my gv">BetaSeed</strong>, a C++-based backdoor malware used by the Kimsuky group. The DLL version of BetaSeed also steals information from the victim system and performs additional malicious actions based on the commands it receives from the C&amp;C server.</p><ul class=""><li id="816b" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">MD5</strong>: d6abeeb469e2417bbcd3c122c06ba099</li><li id="ed5e" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Reference</strong>: <a class="af oq" href="https://asec.ahnlab.com/ko/59209/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">수입 신고서를 위장하여 국내 연구 기관을 노리는 Kimsuky</a></li></ul><p id="19e8" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">However, the 2 malware were separated into different types because they were written in different languages and there were no similarities in the code other than the strings in the function names.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz rz"><picture><source Correlations between backdoor malware used by the Kimsuky group</figcaption></figure><p id="71ab" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">It is noteworthy that GoBear adds SOCKS5 proxy functionality, which was not previously supported by the Kimsuky group’s backdoor malware. Furthermore, the fact that the mutex used in the previous AppleSeed malware was reused after two years without being updated suggests that the author of the Troll Stealer malware based on AppleSeed may have made a mistake.</p><h1 id="18e2" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Conclusion</h1><ul class=""><li id="3411" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">S2W threat research and intelligence center <strong class="my gv">Talon</strong> has hunted for and analyzed a sample of a new malware from the Kimsuky group, and named <strong class="my gv">Troll Stealer</strong>.</li><li id="efd6" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Troll Stealer is written in Go and identified as an Info-stealer malware that steals information from infected systems (SSH, FileZilla, C drive files/directories, browsers, system information, screen captures).<br/> —Troll Stealer is distributed by dropping and executing from a Dropper disguised as SGA Solutions’ Trusted PKI installer.</li><li id="7e14" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">The dropper runs as a legitimate installer alongside the malware, and both the dropper and malware are signed with a <strong class="my gv">valid, legitimate “D2innovation Co.,LTD” certificate</strong>, suggesting that the company’s certificate was actually stolen.</li><li id="493c" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Troll Stealer includes the ability to steal the <strong class="my gv">GPKI</strong> folder on infected systems, which suggests that the campaign may have been targeting devices within administrative and public organizations in South Korea<br/> — The Kimsuky group has no known history of hijacking GPKI folders or utilizing the SOCKS5 protocol in the past, so it is possible that they have set new targets, or that another group with access to the source code for AppleSeed/AlphaSeed created Troll Stealer and GoBear.</li><li id="6972" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">S2W believes that the Kimsuky group is likely behind the distribution of this malware based on the group’s active use of Go-based malware and the many similarities found between Troll Stealer and the existing AppleSeed and AlphaSeed malware.</li><li id="99a3" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">In addition to Troll Stealer, additional malware signed with the same legitimate certificate was found, so it is possible that malware signed with that certificate may be distributed in the future.</li></ul><h1 id="5466" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">MITRE ATT&amp;CK</h1><h2 id="cba2" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">Resource Development</h2><ul class=""><li id="fb6d" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl
